<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- wakaru: to understand, to comprehend

TONE HINT:
- kusuri: medicine

Input: wakatta   wakatta   jy a   sono   kusuri       ima       watashi       kiga atta     nai   desu   kara
Output: /no_think
```

TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- kitsuen: smoking tobacco
- tabako: tobacco, cigarette

TONE HINT:
- aienka: heavy smoker

Input: kitsuen inshu   tabako     arimasu  
Output: /no_think

TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- bisaiundou: fine motor skill, fine motor movement

TONE HINT:
- iwakan: uncomfortable feeling

TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



TONE HINT:
- shinbun: newspaper

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- chuushayaku: injectable drug, injectable medicine

TONE HINT:
- deshouka: don't you think?

Input: kako     ninen   inai     durage u     yakubutsu     ihou   yaku   betsu     shiyou   shita   mata     chuushabari   koto   arimasu     arimasuka

TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").

Output: I have chest pain.

Output: I have no allergies.

TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- kenensareruhen'ishu: variant of concern of SARS-CoV-2, VOC
- seikou: sexual intercourse, sex
- seikinou: sexual function

TONE HINT:
- shoukou: lull

Input:   seikou   shidashi ita   karada     kyou setsu   hannou     shohou   sareta aa   subete kusuru chisai     jikan     fukuyou   shite

<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



TONE HINT:
- kangae: thinking

Input:   mashi   da     kangae   nannin aka       kangae   suru   koto     arimasu  
Output: /no_think
```

- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- zensoku: asthma
- mansei: chronic illness
- shikkan: disease, illness
- haien: pneumonia
- genzai: original sin

TONE HINT:
- genkou: present

Input: genzai   mata   kako       jou       koto   arimasu     zensoku   mansei   heisoku   hai shikkan   haien
Output: /no_think
```

</details>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- shoku: job, work
- hai: yes, that is correct

TONE HINT:
- shokuji: meal

Input: hai   asa       shoku   go   mainichi   nondemasu   uchi   gakkou kara   kaettekite   gohan     warera  tabesasetaki ara   demo   saikin   jibun   amari   agerareru   sugu   onaka     ippai       shimaimasu   sukoshi   taberu   dake     sugu
Output: /no_think
```

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



TONE HINT:
- hakike: nausea

Input: nn nn   hakike   hidoi       hiroki an   dake   desu   ato   yoko       okiagaru   toki     tatte   suwa   tachi   agaru   toki     chotto   memai     desu   onaka     katai   kanji   shite   itsumo   i     itai   desu   senjutsu   kuroi   ben   deta   desu     nani     warui   koto   da     omoi masu

<details>
<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- wakaru: to understand, to comprehend

TONE HINT:
- hizuke: date

Input: wakatta   sensei   kore   ijou   arukadeia   ranai       desu     sugi     youyaku   itsu   desuka   saisho   chichi     hi     happyoukai   aru    
Output: /no_think
```

</details>
